if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'George_Strait';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"george,_,strait,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>George
Harvey
Strait</b>
(born
May
18,
1952)
is
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country
music</a>
singer,
actor
and
music
producer
known
as
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/King_of_Country?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="King
of
Country"
class="mw-redirect">King
of
Country</a>&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-cp_1-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cp-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
one
of
the
most
influential
and
popular
recording
artists
of
all
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-bego_2-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bego-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
is
known
for
his
<a
href="/wiki/Neotraditionalist_country?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Neotraditionalist
country"
class="mw-redirect">neotraditionalist
country</a>
style,
cowboy
look,
and
being
one
of
the
first
and
main
country
artists
to
bring
country
music
back
to
its
roots
and
away
from
the
pop
country
era
in
the
1980s.</p>








<p>Strait's
success
began
when
his
first
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Unwound_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unwound
(song)">Unwound</a>&quot;
was
a
hit
in
1981.
During
the
1980s,
seven
of
his
albums
reached
number
one
on
the
country
charts.
In
the
2000s,
Strait
was
named
Artist
of
the
Decade
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music">Academy
of
Country
Music</a>,
was
elected
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame"
class="mw-redirect">Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>,
and
won
his
first
Grammy
award
for
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Troubadour_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Troubadour
(George
Strait
album)">Troubadour</a></i>.
Strait
was
named
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Association
Awards">CMA</a>
Entertainer
of
the
Year
in
1989,
1990
and
2013,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music">ACM</a>
Entertainer
of
the
Year
in
1990.
He
has
been
nominated
for
more
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Association
Awards">CMA</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music">ACM</a>
awards
and
has
more
wins
in
both
categories
than
any
other
artist.
In
2009,
he
broke
<a
href="/wiki/Conway_Twitty?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Conway
Twitty">Conway
Twitty</a>'s
previous
record
for
the
most
number-one
hits
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a>'</i>s
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Hot
Country
Songs</a>
chart
when
his
44
number
one
singles
surpassed
Twitty's
40.<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
Counting
all
music
charts,
Strait
has
amassed
a
total
of
60
number-one
hits,
breaking
a
record
also
previously
set
by
Twitty.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Strait
has
sold
more
than
70
million
albums
in
the
United
States
and
his
certifications
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>
include
13
multi-platinum,
33
platinum,
and
38
gold
albums.
His
best-selling
album
is
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pure_Country_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pure
Country
(album)">Pure
Country</a></i>
(1992),
which
sold
6
million
(6&times;
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">platinum</a>).
His
highest
certified
album
is
<i><a
href="/wiki/Strait_Out_of_the_Box?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strait
Out
of
the
Box">Strait
Out
of
the
Box</a></i>
(1995),
which
sold
2
million
copies
(8&times;
Platinum
due
to
being
a
box
set
with
four
CDs).
According
to
the
RIAA,
Strait
is
the
12th
best-selling
album
recording
artist
in
the
United
States
overall.</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_life">Early
life</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Strait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
Early
life">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p><b>George
Harvey
Strait</b>
was
born
on
May
18,
1952,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Poteet,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Poteet,
Texas">Poteet</a>,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Atascosa_County,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Atascosa
County,
Texas">Atascosa
County</a>,
south
of
<a
href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="San
Antonio,
Texas"
class="mw-redirect">San
Antonio</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Texas">Texas</a>,
to
John
Byron
Strait,
Sr.
(born
c.
1921
-
died
June
4,
2013),<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
former
Doris
Couser.
He
grew
up
in
<a
href="/wiki/Pearsall,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pearsall,
Texas">Pearsall</a>,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Frio_County,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frio
County,
Texas">Frio
County</a>,
where
his
father
was
a
junior
high
school
mathematics
teacher
and
the
owner
of
a
2,000-acre
(8&nbsp;km&sup2;)
cattle
ranch
outside
of
<a
href="/wiki/Big_Wells,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Big
Wells,
Texas">Big
Wells</a>,
Texas.
The
family
worked
at
the
ranch
on
the
weekends
and
in
the
summers.
When
George
was
in
the
fourth
grade,
his
father
and
mother
were
divorced,
and
his
mother
moved
away
with
his
sister,
Pency.
George
and
his
brother
John,
Jr.,
or
&quot;Buddy&quot;
(1950-2009),
were
reared
by
their
father.<sup
id="cite_ref-cmt_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cmt-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Strait
began
his
musical
interest
while
attending
Pearsall
High
School,
where
he
played
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
roll">rock
and
roll</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Garage_band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garage
band"
class="mw-redirect">garage
band</a>.
His
musical
preference
soon
turned
to
country
with
singers
<a
href="/wiki/Hank_Thompson_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hank
Thompson
(musician)">Hank
Thompson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Lefty_Frizzell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lefty
Frizzell">Lefty
Frizzell</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Merle_Haggard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Merle
Haggard">Merle
Haggard</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/George_Jones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Jones">George
Jones</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Wills?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Wills">Bob
Wills</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Hank_Williams?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hank
Williams">Hank
Williams</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frank
Sinatra">Frank
Sinatra</a>
influencing
his
style.
Strait
did
not
tune
to
the
country
music
radio
often
as
a
youth,
usually
listening
to
the
news
and
the
farmer's
report.
His
introduction
to
country
music
came
mostly
by
way
of
live
performances,
which,
according
to
Strait,
could
be
heard
in
every
town
in
Texas.<sup
id="cite_ref-interview_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-interview-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
eloped
with
his
high
school
sweetheart,
Norma.
The
couple
initially
married
in
<a
href="/wiki/Mexico?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mexico">Mexico</a>
on
December
4,
1971.
That
same
year,
he
enlisted
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_States_Army?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
States
Army">United
States
Army</a>.
While
stationed
at
<a
href="/wiki/Schofield_Barracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Schofield
Barracks">Schofield
Barracks</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Hawaii?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>
as
a
part
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/25th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="25th
Infantry
Division
(United
States)">25th
Infantry
Division</a>,
Strait
began
performing
with
a
U.S.
Army-sponsored
band,
&quot;Rambling
Country&quot;,
which
played
off-base
under
the
name
&quot;Santee&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-cmt_6-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cmt-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
October
6,
1972,
while
still
in
Hawaii,
George
and
Norma
had
their
first
child,
Jenifer.</p>








<p>After
Strait
was
honorably
discharged
from
the
Army
in
1975,
he
enrolled
at
<a
href="/wiki/Southwest_Texas_State_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Southwest
Texas
State
University"
class="mw-redirect">Southwest
Texas
State
University</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/San_Marcos,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="San
Marcos,
Texas">San
Marcos</a>
and
received
a
degree
in
Agriculture.
During
his
college
years,
he
joined
the
country
band
Stoney
Ridge,
answering
a
flyer
the
band
posted
around
campus
looking
for
a
new
vocalist.
Strait
renamed
the
group
the
<a
href="/wiki/Ace_in_the_Hole_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ace
in
the
Hole
Band">Ace
in
the
Hole
Band</a>
and
quickly
became
the
lead;
they
began
to
perform
at
different
honky
tonks
and
bars
around
south
and
central
Texas,
traveling
as
far
east
as
<a
href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Huntsville,
Texas">Huntsville</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Houston,
Texas"
class="mw-redirect">Houston</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-liner_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-liner-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
gained
a
regional
following
and
opened
for
national
acts
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Texas_Playboys?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Texas
Playboys"
class="mw-redirect">The
Texas
Playboys</a>.
Soon,
his
band
was
given
the
opportunity
to
record
several
Strait-penned
singles
including
&quot;That
Don't
Change
The
Way
I
Feel
About
You&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
for
the
Houston-based
D
label.
However,
the
songs
never
achieved
wide
recognition,
and
Strait
continued
to
manage
his
family
cattle
ranch
during
the
day
in
order
to
make
some
extra
cash.<sup
id="cite_ref-liner_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-liner-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-erlewine_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-erlewine-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>While
he
continued
to
play
with
his
band,
without
any
real
connections
to
the
music
industry,
Strait
became
friends
with
Erv
Woolsey,
who
operated
one
of
the
bars
in
which
the
Ace
in
the
Hole
band
played,
and
who
had
previously
worked
for
the
major
label
<a
href="/wiki/MCA_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MCA
Records">MCA
Records</a>.
Woolsey
convinced
some
of
his
<a
href="/wiki/Music_Row?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
Row">Music
Row</a>
(Nashville,
TN)
connections
to
come
to
Texas
and
to
listen
to
Strait
and
his
band
play.
Impressed
with
the
performance,
MCA
quickly
signed
Strait
to
a
recording
contract
in
February
1981.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
Ace
in
the
Hole
band
remained
with
Strait,
performing
as
the
backup
and
touring
band
for
the
now
solo
act.<sup
id="cite_ref-erlewine_10-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-erlewine-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_career">Music
career</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Strait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Music
career">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1980s">1980s</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Strait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
1980s">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
the
spring
of
1981,
Strait
released
his
first
single
for
MCA
Records,
entitled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Unwound_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Unwound
(song)">Unwound</a>&quot;,
which
climbed
into
the
top
ten
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Hot
Country
Songs</a>
chart
that
year,
and
was
included
on
his
debut
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Strait_Country?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strait
Country">Strait
Country</a></i>.
The
record
featured
two
more
singles
including
&quot;Down
and
Out&quot;,
a
No.&nbsp;16
hit
for
Strait,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/If_You%27re_Thinking_You_Want_a_Stranger_(There%27s_One_Coming_Home)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="If
You're
Thinking
You
Want
a
Stranger
(There's
One
Coming
Home)">If
You're
Thinking
You
Want
a
Stranger
(There's
One
Coming
Home)</a>&quot;,
which
reached
number
three
early
in
1982,
sparking
a
string
of
Top
Ten
hits
that
ran
well
into
the
1990s.<sup
id="cite_ref-George_Strait_biography_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-George_Strait_biography-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Strait
Country</i>
was
hailed
by
critics
as
a
traditionalist
breakthrough
that
broke
the
trend
of
pop-influenced
country
prevalent
at
the
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
year
1982
also
saw
the
release
of
Strait's
second
album,
the
critically
acclaimed
<i><a
href="/wiki/Strait_from_the_Heart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strait
from
the
Heart">Strait
from
the
Heart</a></i>,
which
featured
the
first
number
one
single
of
his
career,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Fool_Hearted_Memory?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fool
Hearted
Memory">Fool
Hearted
Memory</a>&quot;,
and
the
top
five
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Amarillo_by_Morning_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Amarillo
by
Morning
(song)">Amarillo
by
Morning</a>&quot;,
regarded
by
many
as
one
of
the
greatest
country
songs
of
all-time.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1983,
Strait
made
his
first
appearance
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Houston_Livestock_Show_and_Rodeo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Houston
Livestock
Show
and
Rodeo">Houston
Livestock
Show
and
Rodeo</a>
when
the
headlining
star,
Eddie
Rabbitt,
came
down
sick
with
the
flu.
Strait
has
since
become
a
mainstay
throughout
his
career,
making
more
than
twenty
appearances
at
the
Rodeo,
and
playing
to
a
total
of
more
than
one
million
fans.
Strait
recorded
17
subsequent
No.&nbsp;1's
in
the
decade,
including
a
string
of
five
that
lasted
from
1983–84<sup
id="cite_ref-lp_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lp-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
from
his
next
two
albums
<i><a
href="/wiki/Right_or_Wrong_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Right
or
Wrong
(George
Strait
album)">Right
or
Wrong</a></i>,
his
first
number
one
album
and
the
CMA
award-winning
<i><a
href="/wiki/Does_Fort_Worth_Ever_Cross_Your_Mind?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Does
Fort
Worth
Ever
Cross
Your
Mind">Does
Fort
Worth
Ever
Cross
Your
Mind</a></i>.
The
next
year,
he
won
the
CMA
award
for
top
male
vocalist,
and
released
his
first
<a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
Hits
(George
Strait
album)">Greatest
hits
compilation</a>,
which
featured
songs
from
his
first
three
albums.
Also
in
1985,
Strait
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Something_Special_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Something
Special
(George
Strait
album)">Something
Special</a></i>,
the
third
straight
number-one
album
of
his
career,
featuring
the
number-one
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Chair_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Chair
(song)">The
Chair</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1986,
Strait
repeated
as
the
CMA
vocalist
of
the
year
and
released
his
fourth
No.&nbsp;1
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/7_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="7
(George
Strait
album)">#7</a></i>.
Strait
and
his
family
were
struck
with
tragedy
when
his
13-year-old
daughter,
Jenifer,
was
killed
in
a
one-car
non-alcohol-related
accident.
She
was
riding
in
a
Ford
Mustang
driven
by
Gregory
Wilson
Allen,
18,
of
Staples,
Texas.
He
was
subsequently
charged
with
a
Class
A
misdemeanor
for
vehicular
homicide.
Mike
Cox,
spokesman
for
the
Texas
Department
of
Public
Safety
in
Austin,
said
&quot;The
responding
trooper
determined
the
cause
of
accident
to
be
excessive
speed
and
that
the
car
did
not
negotiate
the
turn
properly.
Jenifer
was
riding
in
the
front
passengers
seat
and
none
of
the
four
occupants
were
wearing
seat
belts
at
the
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
the
vehicle
flipped
over
onto
its
passenger's
side,
Jenifer
was
partially
ejected,
causing
her
to
be
dead
upon
impact.
The
incident
did
not
hinder
Strait's
performance,
as
he
went
on
to
release
11
straight
No.&nbsp;1
hits,
starting
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Nobody_in_His_Right_Mind_Would%27ve_Left_Her?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nobody
in
His
Right
Mind
Would've
Left
Her">Nobody
in
His
Right
Mind
Would've
Left
Her</a>&quot;
in
1986
and
ending
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Ace_in_the_Hole_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ace
in
the
Hole
(George
Strait
song)">Ace
in
the
Hole</a>&quot;
in
1989.<sup
id="cite_ref-lp_16-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lp-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
singles
spanned
four
albums,
including
<i>#7</i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ocean_Front_Property?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ocean
Front
Property">Ocean
Front
Property</a></i>
in
1987,
<i><a
href="/wiki/If_You_Ain%27t_Lovin%27_You_Ain%27t_Livin%27?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="If
You
Ain't
Lovin'
You
Ain't
Livin'">If
You
Ain't
Lovin'
You
Ain't
Livin'</a></i>
in
1988
and
1989's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Beyond_the_Blue_Neon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Beyond
the
Blue
Neon">Beyond
the
Blue
Neon</a></i>,
all
of
which
reached
the
number
one
spot
on
country
album
charts.
<i>Ocean
Front
Property</i>
was
the
first
country
album
to
ever
debut
at
No.&nbsp;1
on
the
charts
by
any
artist.
The
streak
included
such
songs
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Ocean_Front_Property_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ocean
Front
Property
(song)">Ocean
Front
Property</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_My_Ex%27s_Live_in_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="All
My
Ex's
Live
in
Texas">All
My
Ex's
Live
in
Texas</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Famous_Last_Words_of_a_Fool?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Famous
Last
Words
of
a
Fool">Famous
Last
Words
of
a
Fool</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Baby_Blue_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Baby
Blue
(George
Strait
song)">Baby
Blue</a>&quot;,
which
is
rumored
to
have
been
dedicated
to
his
daughter.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
Strait
finished
the
decade
by
winning
the
CMA
Entertainer
of
the
Year
award
in
1989.
A
year
later,
he
won
the
award
again.<sup
id="cite_ref-George_Strait_biography_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-George_Strait_biography-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="1990s">1990s</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Strait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
1990s">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:George_Strait_on_stage.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/George_Strait_on_stage.jpg/220px-George_Strait_on_stage.jpg"
width="220"
height="330"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/George_Strait_on_stage.jpg/330px-George_Strait_on_stage.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/George_Strait_on_stage.jpg/440px-George_Strait_on_stage.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:George_Strait_on_stage.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
George
Strait
performing
live
at
the
Mariner
Arena,
Baltimore,
Maryland
on
April
7,
2008









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Strait
began
the
decade
with
the
release
of
his
tenth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Livin%27_It_Up_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Livin'
It
Up
(album)">Livin'
It
Up</a></i>,
which
featured
two
No.&nbsp;1
hits
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Love_Without_End,_Amen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Love
Without
End,
Amen">Love
Without
End,
Amen</a>&quot;,
his
first
multi-week
hit,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I%27ve_Come_to_Expect_It_From_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I've
Come
to
Expect
It
From
You"
class="mw-redirect">I've
Come
to
Expect
It
From
You</a>&quot;.
Both
songs
remained
No.&nbsp;1
for
five
weeks
in
1990.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Chill_of_an_Early_Fall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chill
of
an
Early
Fall">Chill
of
an
Early
Fall</a></i>
shortly
followed
in
1991,
and
received
positive
reviews.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Entertainment
Weekly">Entertainment
Weekly</a></i>
noted
that
the
album
marked
a
shift
for
Strait
from
&quot;repeating
himself&quot;
in
his
previous
works
to
producing
different
material.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
produced
the
No.&nbsp;1's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/If_I_Know_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="If
I
Know
Me">If
I
Know
Me</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Know_Me_Better_Than_That?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Know
Me
Better
Than
That">You
Know
Me
Better
Than
That</a>&quot;,
but
ended
his
streak
of
31
straight
top
ten
hits
with
the
cover
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lovesick_Blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lovesick
Blues">Lovesick
Blues</a>&quot;,
which
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;24.<sup
id="cite_ref-lp_16-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lp-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
record
blocked
his
run
of
eight
top
charting
albums
with
its
peak
of
No.&nbsp;4.
In
the
spring
of
1992,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Holding_My_Own?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Holding
My
Own">Holding
My
Own</a></i>
was
released.
It
did
not
produce
any
No.&nbsp;1s
but
did
include
two
top
five
songs
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/So_Much_Like_My_Dad?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="So
Much
Like
My
Dad">So
Much
Like
My
Dad</a>&quot;.
Later
in
1992,
Strait
played
the
main
character
in
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pure_Country?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pure
Country">Pure
Country</a></i>,
and
released
the
film's
soundtrack.
It
was
his
most
successful
studio
album,
producing
such
hits
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Heartland_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heartland
(George
Strait
song)">Heartland</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Cross_My_Heart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Cross
My
Heart">I
Cross
My
Heart</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/When_Did_You_Stop_Loving_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="When
Did
You
Stop
Loving
Me">When
Did
You
Stop
Loving
Me</a>&quot;,
and
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;1
and
No.&nbsp;6
respectively
on
the
Country
and
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200">Billboard
200</a>
album
charts.
The
success
continued
with
his
next
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Easy_Come,_Easy_Go_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Easy
Come,
Easy
Go
(George
Strait
album)">Easy
Come,
Easy
Go</a></i>
in
1993,
which
reached
the
top
five
on
the
Billboard
200
and
featured
the
hits
&quot;I'd
Like
to
Have
That
One
Back&quot;,
&quot;The
Man
in
Love
with
You&quot;,
and
the
No.&nbsp;1
title
track.
His
next
four
albums,
including
<i><a
href="/wiki/Lead_On?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lead
On">Lead
On</a></i>
in
1994,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blue_Clear_Sky?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blue
Clear
Sky">Blue
Clear
Sky</a></i>
in
1996,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Carrying_Your_Love_with_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carrying
Your
Love
with
Me">Carrying
Your
Love
with
Me</a></i>
in
1997,
and
1998's
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_Step_at_a_Time_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Step
at
a
Time
(George
Strait
album)">One
Step
at
a
Time</a></i>,
all
charted
at
No.&nbsp;1,
with
<i>Blue
Clear
Sky</i>
claiming
the
spot
on
its
debut
week,
and
<i>Carrying
Your
Love
with
Me</i>
peaking
at
No.&nbsp;1
on
the
Billboard
200
for
the
first
time
in
Strait's
career.
This
series
of
albums
produced
eight
number
one
singles
for
Strait,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Can%27t_Make_a_Heart_Love_Somebody?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Can't
Make
a
Heart
Love
Somebody">You
Can't
Make
a
Heart
Love
Somebody</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Carried_Away_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carried
Away
(George
Strait
song)">Carried
Away</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/One_Night_at_a_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Night
at
a
Time">One
Night
at
a
Time</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Just_Want_to_Dance_with_You?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Just
Want
to
Dance
with
You">I
Just
Want
to
Dance
with
You</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-George_Strait_biography_12-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-George_Strait_biography-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
During
this
period,
Strait
also
released
a
four-disc
box
set
career
retrospective,
<i>Strait
Out
of
the
Box</i>,
in
1995,
which
became
the
second-best-selling
box
set
ever
with
shipments
of
8
million
in
the
United
States.
He
also
was
named
as
the
CMA's
Top
Male
Vocalist
in
1997
and
1998.<sup
id="cite_ref-erlewine_10-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-erlewine-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Starting
in
'97,
and
continuing
until
the
first
year
of
the
21st
century,
Strait
headlined
the
George
Strait
Country
Music
Festival,
which
included
artists
such
has
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_McGraw?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
McGraw">Tim
McGraw</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Faith_Hill?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Faith
Hill">Faith
Hill</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Kenny_Chesney?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kenny
Chesney">Kenny
Chesney</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Alan_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alan
Jackson">Alan
Jackson</a>,
and
others.
In
an
effort
to
introduce
these
acts
to
as
many
fans
as
possible,
the
festival
promised
not
to
visit
any
market
more
than
twice.
It
played
only
a
small
number
of
dates,
usually
no
more
than
twenty
a
year,
but
still
managed
to
be
the
ninth-biggest-grossing
tour
of
1998.
In
2009,
the
George
Strait
Country
Music
Festival
was
voted
the
most
important
tour
in
the
history
of
country
music
and
the
best
selling
country
music
tour
in
the
90s
.<sup
id="cite_ref-tafoya_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tafoya-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Strait
completed
the
decade
with
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Always_Never_the_Same_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Always
Never
the
Same
(George
Strait
album)">Always
Never
the
Same</a></i>
in
1999,
which
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;2
on
country
charts
and
matched
the
cross-over
success
of
<i>Pure
Country</i>
by
reaching
No.&nbsp;6
on
the
Billboard
200.
The
record
produced
the
hits
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What_Do_You_Say_to_That?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What
Do
You
Say
to
That">What
Do
You
Say
to
That</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Meanwhile_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Meanwhile
(song)">Meanwhile</a>&quot;,
and
the
No.&nbsp;1
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Write_This_Down_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Write
This
Down
(song)">Write
This
Down</a>&quot;.
Reviews
of
the
album's
material
were
generally
moderate,
but
<i>Entertainment
Weekly</i>
observed
that
at
this
point
in
his
career,
Strait
could
record
the
&quot;most
lightweight&quot;
material
and
&quot;make
it
soar&quot;
on
the
radio
with
his
&quot;grace&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
All
in
all,
Strait
scored
17
No.
1
hits
on
the
Billboard
country
airplay
charts
in
the
decade,
and
carried
his
successes
into
the
next
century.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

–

<span

–
present">edit</a>]</span></h3>

<p>Strait
released
a
<a
href="/wiki/George_Strait_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
Strait
(album)">self-named
album</a>
in
2000,
which
despite
a
No.&nbsp;1
and
No.&nbsp;7
showing
on
the
country
and
Billboard
200
album
charts,
produced
no
No.&nbsp;1
singles,
and
was
the
first
studio
album
of
his
career
to
not
be
certified
as
platinum.
The
singles
&quot;Go
On&quot;
and
&quot;If
You
Can
Do
Anything
Else&quot;
were
released
from
the
record,
with
both
peaking
in
the
top
five.
In
May
2001,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Road_Less_Traveled_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Road
Less
Traveled
(George
Strait
album)">The
Road
Less
Traveled</a></i>
was
released.
Reviews
for
the
album
were
mostly
positive,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
described
it
as
sticking
to
the
formula
&quot;but
adds
a
few
twists
that
make
it
superior
to
his
last
few
releases.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
featured
&quot;vocal
processing,&quot;
and
was
considered
by
some
critics
as
an
experimental
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-erlewine_10-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-erlewine-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
Three
singles
were
released
from
it,
two
of
which
reached
No.&nbsp;1,
including
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She%27ll_Leave_You_with_a_Smile?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="She'll
Leave
You
with
a
Smile">She'll
Leave
You
with
a
Smile</a>&quot;,
his
50th
on
combined
charts
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Living_and_Living_Well?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Living
and
Living
Well">Living
and
Living
Well</a>&quot;,
both
of
which
reached
the
top
30
of
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100">Billboard
Hot
100</a>,
with
the
former
peaking
at
No.&nbsp;23,
Strait's
highest
rank
on
the
chart.
The
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Run_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Run
(George
Strait
song)">Run</a>&quot;
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;2
and
reached
No.&nbsp;34
on
the
Billboard
100.
Strait
released
two
records
in
2003.
<i><a
href="/wiki/For_the_Last_Time:_Live_from_the_Astrodome?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="For
the
Last
Time:
Live
from
the
Astrodome">For
the
Last
Time:
Live
from
the
Astrodome</a></i>
was
a
recording
of
the
last
Houston
Livestock
Show
and
Rodeo
to
take
place
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Astrodome?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Astrodome"
class="mw-redirect">Astrodome</a>.
The
performance
itself,
set
the
record
for
paid
attendance
at
the
venue,
with
68,266
people,
breaking
Latin
superstar
<a
href="/wiki/Selena?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Selena">Selena</a>'s
previous
record
of
approximately
67,000
in
1995.
His
next
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Honkytonkville?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Honkytonkville">Honkytonkville</a></i>
was
described
as
&quot;a
fiery
set
of
hard
country&quot;,
and
was
praised
&quot;for
its
mixture
of
the
old
Strait
with
his
modern,
superstar
self.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-erlewine_10-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-erlewine-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
didn't
produce
any
No.&nbsp;1's
for
Strait
but
included
the
hits
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cowboys_Like_Us?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cowboys
Like
Us">Cowboys
Like
Us</a>&quot;
and
a
cover
of
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Robison?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Robison">Bruce
Robison</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Desperately_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Desperately
(George
Strait
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Desperately</a>&quot;.
His
2004
performance
at
Reliant
Stadium
set
a
new
Rodeo
attendance
record,
with
68,679
spectators.
That
year
he
issued
a
Greatest
Hits
package
billed
as
<a
href="/wiki/50_Number_Ones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50
Number
Ones">50
Number
Ones</a>,
chronicalling
the
No.&nbsp;1
hits
of
his
career
from
all
charts,
starting
with
&quot;Fool
Hearted
Memory&quot;
and
ending
with
&quot;She'll
Leave
You
With
a
Smile.&quot;
The
next
year,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Somewhere_Down_in_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Somewhere
Down
in
Texas">Somewhere
Down
in
Texas</a></i>
arrived,
which
produced
the
hit
&quot;You'll
Be
There,&quot;
marking
Strait's
first
appearance
on
the
Adult
Contemporary
chart.
The
next
year,
he
embarked
on
a
tour
that
included
only
18
performances
but
grossed
over
$15
million.
He
attributed
this
success
to
the
fact
that
he
and
his
band
are
&quot;musically
very
tight,&quot;
have
a
large
pool
of
songs
to
draw
from,
and
perform
those
songs
very
similarly
to
how
they
sound
on
their
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-stark_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-stark-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>On
October
3,
2006,
Strait
marked
his
30th
year
in
the
music
industry
with
the
release
of
a
new
album
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/It_Just_Comes_Natural?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It
Just
Comes
Natural">It
Just
Comes
Natural</a></i>.
It
featured
fifteen
new
songs.
Strait's
long-time
friend
and
songwriter,
<a
href="/wiki/Dean_Dillon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dean
Dillon">Dean
Dillon</a>
co-wrote
two
of
the
songs
on
the
album.
It
received
generally
positive
reviews
from
critics.
<i><a
href="/wiki/People_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People
(magazine)">People</a></i>,
in
their
four-star
review,
remarked
that
&quot;If
ever
there
was
a
natural
in
country
music,
it's
Strait,&quot;
while
<i><a
href="/wiki/USA_Today?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="USA
Today">USA
Today</a></i>
raved
that
&quot;he
continues
to
make
such
consistent
quality
look
easy.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-nashvillehype_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nashvillehype-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
single
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Give_It_Away_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Give
It
Away
(George
Strait
song)">Give
It
Away</a>&quot;
reached
No.&nbsp;1
and
the
title
track,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/It_Just_Comes_Natural_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It
Just
Comes
Natural
(song)">It
Just
Comes
Natural</a>&quot;
became
his
42nd
Billboard
No.&nbsp;1.
In
2007,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wrapped_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wrapped
(George
Strait
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Wrapped</a>&quot;
reached
No.
1
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mediabase_24/7?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mediabase
24/7"
class="mw-redirect">Mediabase
24/7</a>
country
music
charts,
giving
Strait
his
55th
overall
number-one
single.
From
January
through
April
of
that
year,
Strait
headlined
a
23-date
arena
tour
with
country
music
legend
<a
href="/wiki/Ronnie_Milsap?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronnie
Milsap">Ronnie
Milsap</a>
and
newcomer
<a
href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Taylor
Swift">Taylor
Swift</a>.
He
released
a
new
album
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Troubadour_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Troubadour
(George
Strait
album)">Troubadour</a></i>
on
April
1,
2008.
The
CD
contained
12
tracks,
including
a
duet
with
<a
href="/wiki/Patty_Loveless?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Patty
Loveless">Patty
Loveless</a>
and
another
with
long-time
songwriter
<a
href="/wiki/Dean_Dillon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dean
Dillon">Dean
Dillon</a>.
The
lead
single
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Saw_God_Today?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Saw
God
Today">I
Saw
God
Today</a>&quot;,
debuted
at
No.&nbsp;19
on
the
Radio
and
Records
and
Billboard
charts.
It
is
the
highest
debut
ever
for
a
single
from
Strait
and
the
fourth
highest
debut
for
a
song
in
country
music
history.
<i>Troubadour</i>
debuted
at
No.&nbsp;1
on
the
Billboard
Top
200
album
charts,
selling
over
160,000
copies
in
its
first
week
of
release.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/River_of_Love?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="River
of
Love">River
of
Love</a>&quot;
the
3rd
single
from
the
album
became
his
57th
number-one
song
in
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-cmt-morris_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cmt-morris-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In
April
2009,
George
Strait
was
honored
by
the
Academy
of
Country
Music
with
the
Artist
of
the
Decade
Award,
which
was
presented
to
Strait
by
the
previous
ACM
Artist
of
the
Decade,
Garth
Brooks.
In
June
of
that
year
he
headlined
the
first
event
at
the
new
Dallas
<a
href="/wiki/Cowboys_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cowboys
Stadium"
class="mw-redirect">Cowboys
Stadium</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Arlington,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Arlington,
Texas">Arlington,
Texas</a>.
Strait's
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Living_for_the_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Living
for
the
Night">Living
for
the
Night</a>&quot;
was
released
on
May
28,
2009,
and
was
written
by
Strait,
his
son
Bubba,
and
Dean
Dillon.
The
song
was
the
lead
single
from
his
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Twang_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Twang
(album)">Twang</a></i>,
released
on
August
11,
2009.
<i>Twang</i>
was
certified
gold
for
selling
over
500,000
copies.
In
2010,
Billboard
ranked
Strait
No.&nbsp;1
in
the
top
25
country
artists
of
the
past
25
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
September
6,
2011,
Strait
released
the
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Here_for_a_Good_Time_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Here
for
a
Good
Time
(album)"
class="mw-redirect">Here
for
a
Good
Time</a></i>,
which
yielded
two
No.&nbsp;1
singles—&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Here_for_a_Good_Time_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Here
for
a
Good
Time
(song)">Here
for
a
Good
Time</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Love%27s_Gonna_Make_It_Alright?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Love's
Gonna
Make
It
Alright">Love's
Gonna
Make
It
Alright</a>&quot;—bringing
Strait's
No.&nbsp;1
singles
total
to
59.
The
album's
third
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Drinkin%27_Man?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drinkin'
Man">Drinkin'
Man</a>&quot;,
was
less
successful,
peaking
at
No.&nbsp;37.</p>








<p>In
October
2012,
Strait
released
a
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Give_It_All_We_Got_Tonight?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Give
It
All
We
Got
Tonight">Give
It
All
We
Got
Tonight</a>&quot;,<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
which
was
included
on
his
current
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Love_Is_Everything_(George_Strait_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Love
Is
Everything
(George
Strait
album)">Love
Is
Everything</a></i>,
released
on
May
14,
2013.
The
song
initiated
a
&quot;60
for
60&quot;
movement
by
Strait's
label,
to
make
the
song
his
sixtieth
number-one
single
on
all
country
charts
while
he
was
still
60
years
old.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
reached
the
top
of
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Mediabase?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mediabase">Mediabase</a></i>
charts
in
May
2013.
The
album's
next
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Believe_(George_Strait_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Believe
(George
Strait
song)">I
Believe</a>&quot;
reached
No.&nbsp;50
on
The
U.S.
Country
Airplay
chart,
making
it
Strait's
first
single
to
miss
the
Top
40.
Strait
won
the
2013
CMA
Entertainer
of
the
Year
award.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_Cowboy_Rides_Away_Tour">The
Cowboy
Rides
Away
Tour</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Strait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
The
Cowboy
Rides
Away
Tour">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/The_Cowboy_Rides_Away_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Cowboy
Rides
Away
Tour">The
Cowboy
Rides
Away
Tour</a>







</div>








<p>On
September
26,
2012,
Strait
announced
that
he
was
retiring
from
touring,
and
that
his
Cowboy
Rides
Away
Tour
would
be
his
last.<sup
id="cite_ref-cowboy-rides-away_31-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cowboy-rides-away-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
started
on
January
18,
2013
in
Lubbock,
Texas
and
is
divided
into
two
legs:
21
concerts
in
2013
and
26
concerts
in
2014,
for
a
total
of
47
concerts.
The
tour
is
scheduled
to
end
in
Dallas,
Texas
on
June
7,
2014.
Strait
is
supported
on
the
tour
by
his
longtime
eleven-member
touring
group,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Ace_in_the_Hole_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ace
in
the
Hole
Band">Ace
in
the
Hole
Band</a>.
For
the
2013
leg,
<a
href="/wiki/Martina_McBride?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Martina
McBride">Martina
McBride</a>
was
the
opening
performer.<sup
id="cite_ref-cowboy-rides-away_31-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cowboy-rides-away-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
January
9,
2014,
Strait
initiated
the
second
leg
of
his
Cowboy
Rides
Away
Tour,
which
will
include
26
concerts.</p>

<p>In
1981,
George
and
Norma's
son,
George
Strait,
Jr.,
known
as
&quot;Bubba&quot;,
was
born.
Their
daughter
Jenifer
(born
October
6,
1972)
was
killed
in
an
automobile
accident
in
San
Marcos
on
June
25,
1986,
at
the
age
of
13.
The
family
set
up
the
Jenifer
Lynn
Strait
Foundation,
which
donates
money
to
children's
charities
in
the
San
Antonio
area.<sup
id="cite_ref-racheljoyscott_34-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-racheljoyscott-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bubba,
who
is
a
graduate
of
<a
href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Texas
A&amp;M
University">Texas
A&amp;M</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/College_Station,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="College
Station,
Texas">College
Station</a>,
is
pursuing
a
career
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Professional_Rodeo_Cowboys_Association?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Professional
Rodeo
Cowboys
Association">Professional
Rodeo
Cowboys
Association</a>
(PRCA)
team
roping
competitor.<sup
id="cite_ref-straitheir_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-straitheir-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
Strait
was
able
to
watch
his
son
compete
at
the
Houston
Livestock
Show
and
Rodeo
in
2006
shortly
before
taking
the
stage
for
his
own
performance.</p>








<p>Strait
enjoys
hunting,
fishing,
skiing,
playing
golf,
and
riding
motorcycles.
Along
with
his
son,
he
is
a
member
of
the
PRCA
and
partners
in
team
roping
competitions.
George
and
his
elder
brother
John
Jr.,
known
as
Buddy,
hosted
the
annual
<i>George
Strait
Team
Roping
Classic</i>,
in
which
they
competed
against
some
of
the
best
team
ropers
in
the
world.
Strait
has
also
said
that
he
very
seldom
picks
up
a
guitar
when
not
in
the
studio
or
touring.
He
and
his
wife
live
in
far
northwest
San
Antonio
in
the
wealthy
gated
community,
The
Dominion,
as
well
as
on
a
ranch
near
<a
href="/wiki/Cotulla,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cotulla,
Texas">Cotulla</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/La_Salle_County,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="La
Salle
County,
Texas">La
Salle
County</a>
between
San
Antonio
and
<a
href="/wiki/Laredo,_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Laredo,
Texas">Laredo</a>.
Strait
is
a
fan
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Basketball
Association">NBA</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/San_Antonio_Spurs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="San
Antonio
Spurs">San
Antonio
Spurs</a>
and
can
be
seen
court-side
at
many
of
the
Spurs'
home
basketball
games.</p>








<p>Since
2010,
Strait
has
served
as
spokesman
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Wrangler_(jeans)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wrangler
(jeans)">Wrangler</a>
National
Patriot
program,
a
campaign
designed
to
raise
awareness
and
funds
for
America's
wounded
and
fallen
military
veterans
and
their
families.<sup
id="cite_ref-wranglerpatriot_36-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wranglerpatriot-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-vets_37-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vets-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
Strait
states,
&quot;I've
been
a
part
of
the
Wrangler
family
for
a
long
time...
when
they
came
to
me
with
the
idea
for
supporting
fallen
and
wounded
American
veterans
and
their
families,
I
knew
I
wanted
to
get
involved.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-vets_37-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vets-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
February
2012,
Strait
became
a
grandfather,
as
his
son
George
Strait,
Jr.,
and
his
wife,
Tamara,
had
their
first
child,
a
son.
According
to
reports,
the
infant
was
named
George
H.
Strait,
III,
as
a
tribute
to
his
famous
grandfather.<sup
id="cite_ref-after_38-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-after-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
grandson
is
known
as
Harvey,
from
his
common
middle
name
shared
with
his
father
and
grandfather.</p>








<p>George
Strait
owns
a
<a
href="/wiki/Bombardier_Challenger_300?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bombardier
Challenger
300">Bombardier
Challenger
300</a>
jet,
MSN
20132,
and
carries
a
personal
registration
N518GS.
His
personal
aircraft
is
housed
at
the
Landmark
Aviation
facility
in
San
Antonio.<sup
id="cite_ref-plane_39-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-plane-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Strait
was
reared
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Baptist_Church?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Baptist
Church"
class="mw-redirect">Baptist
Church</a>.
He
is
believed
to
be
a
<a
href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Republican
Party
(United
States)">Republican</a>
but
does
not
discuss
political
issues
in
public.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In
more
than
30
years
of
recording,
all
of
which
have
been
spent
with
MCA
Records,
George
Strait
has
garnered
60
No.
1
songs
on
all
country
charts
(including
<a
href="/wiki/Mediabase_24/7?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mediabase
24/7"
class="mw-redirect">Mediabase
24/7</a>,
the
former
<a
href="/wiki/Radio_%26_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radio
&amp;
Records">Radio
&amp;
Records</a>
chart,
and
the
now-defunct
Gavin
Report
chart),
and
has
more
No.&nbsp;1
hits
than
any
other
artist
in
any
genre.
His
44
<i>Billboard</i>
magazine
country
No.
1's
are
a
record,
four
more
than
Conway
Twitty's
total
that
includes
several
duets
with
<a
href="/wiki/Loretta_Lynn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loretta
Lynn">Loretta
Lynn</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-stark_25-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-stark-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
Additionally,
Strait
is
also
the
first
artist
in
the
history
of
<i>Billboard</i>
magazine
to
have
at
least
one
single
enter
the
Top
10
of
a
<i>Billboard</i>
chart
for
30
consecutive
years,
starting
in
1981
when
his
debut
single
&quot;Unwound&quot;
peaked
at
No.&nbsp;6
on
the
Hot
Country
Singles
chart.
All
of
his
Top
10
singles
have
been
on
that
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup>
Strait
has
sold
more
than
68
million
albums
in
the
United
States<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
his
certifications
from
the
RIAA
include
13
multi-platinum,
33
platinum,
and
38
gold
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Filmography">Filmography</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Strait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Filmography">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>Strait
has
acted
in
several
films.
He
had
a
<a
href="/wiki/Bit_part?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bit
part">bit
part</a>
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Soldier_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Soldier
(film)">The
Soldier</a></i>
(1982)
and
starred
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Pure_Country_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pure
Country
(film)"
class="mw-redirect">Pure
Country</a></i>
(1992).
He
also
appeared
as
himself
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/Grand_Champion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grand
Champion">Grand
Champion</a></i>
(2002).</p>








<p>The
film
<i>Pure
Country</i>
featured
George
Strait
in
the
lead
role
as
Dusty
Chandler,
a
famous
country
singer
who
strays
too
far
from
his
country
roots
and
traditional
sound.
It
provided
the
opportunity
for
Strait
to
branch
out
from
his
own
traditional
country
sound
for
a
more
rock-and-roll
approach.
The
film
saw
little
success
at
the
box
office,
taking
in
only
$15
million,
but
the
soundtrack,
also
called
<i>Pure
Country</i>,
produced
several
hit
singles
for
Strait,
and
has
become
his
best-selling
album
to
date.
Strait
had
a
limited
role
in
the
sequel
to
<i>Pure
Country</i>,
<i>Pure
Country
2:
The
Gift</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

in

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Awards">Awards</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=George_Strait&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Awards">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hall_of_Fame_Rotunda.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hall_of_Fame_Rotunda.jpg/220px-Hall_of_Fame_Rotunda.jpg"
width="220"
height="293"
class="thumbimage"

http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Hall_of_Fame_Rotunda.jpg/440px-Hall_of_Fame_Rotunda.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hall_of_Fame_Rotunda.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"

/></a>










</div>
George
Strait











<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame"
class="mw-redirect">Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
plaque









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Strait
holds
the
record
for
most
number
one
albums,
gold
albums,
platinum
albums,
and
multi-platinum
in
the
history
of
country
music,
and
is
eleventh
in
the
most
number
one
albums
in
all
other
genres.
Strait
is
third
only
to
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elvis
Presley">Elvis
Presley</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>
with
the
most
gold
and
platinum
albums
in
the
history
of
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-boot_45-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-boot-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
Strait
has
been
certified
as
the
twelfth
best
selling
artist
in
American
history,
with
career
album
sales
of
70
million.<sup
id="cite_ref-gather_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gather-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Strait
has
recorded
the
most
number
one
songs
and
top
five
songs
in
the
history
of
music
of
any
kind,
and
is
the
only
artist
in
the
history
of
music
of
any
kind
to
have
a
top
ten
hit
every
year
for
thirty
years.
He
is
also
second
all-time
in
top
ten
hits
in
the
history
of
music,
currently
5
away
from
breaking
the
all
time
record
held
by
<a
href="/wiki/Eddy_Arnold?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eddy
Arnold">Eddy
Arnold</a>
who
had
92
in
his
historic
career.
Strait
has
also
won
22
<a
href="/wiki/CMA_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CMA
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">CMA
Awards</a>,
including
consecutive
Entertainer
of
the
Year
honors
in
1989
and
1990,
and
also
just
recently
won
that
same
honor
in
2013
and
holds
the
career
record
for
CMA
nominations
(as
a
whole)
and
the
most
consecutively
of
all
time.As
of
2009
he
holds
the
record
for
the
most
CMA
awards.
Strait
also
holds
those
same
records
for
wins
and
nominations
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/ACM_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ACM
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">ACM
Awards</a>.
Strait
was
elected
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame"
class="mw-redirect">Country
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2006,
performing
his
then-latest
No.
1
hit
&quot;Give
it
Away&quot;
right
before
accepting
his
replica
Hall
of
Fame
plaque
at
the
40th
CMA
Awards.
He
was
only
the
second
artist
(after
<a
href="/wiki/Eddy_Arnold?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eddy
Arnold">Eddy
Arnold</a>
in
1966)
to
be
inducted
into
the
Hall
of
Fame
while
still
actively
recording
and
producing
chart-topping
hits
and
albums.</p>








<p>As
of
June
8,
2010,
George
Strait
was
named
the
top
country
music
artist
of
the
past
25
years
according
to
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_magazine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
magazine"
class="mw-redirect">Billboard
magazine</a>.
In
October
2008,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards">Academy
of
Country
Music
Awards</a>
named
Strait
their
Artist
of
the
Decade
for
the
2000s.
He
was
presented
the
award
by
the
previous
winner
Garth
Brooks.
Past
winners
of
the
award
are
<a
href="/wiki/Marty_Robbins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marty
Robbins">Marty
Robbins</a>
(1960s),
<a
href="/wiki/Loretta_Lynn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loretta
Lynn">Loretta
Lynn</a>
(1970s),
<a
href="/wiki/Alabama_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alabama
(band)">Alabama</a>
(1980s)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Garth_Brooks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garth
Brooks">Garth
Brooks</a>
(1990s).<sup
id="cite_ref-gs-awards_47-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gs-awards-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
And
with
the
win
of
the
entertainer
of
the
year
award
in
2013
he
is
the
only
artist
to
ever
win
the
entertainer
of
the
year
in
three
different
decades
and
also
was
the
oldest
winner.
The
win
is
currently
the
longest
span
between
wins
for
that
award
as
well.
Strait
is
also
tied
with
Merle
Haggard
for
the
most
male
vocalist
of
the
year
awards.
In
2013
billboard
magazine
nominated
Strait
for
its
biggest
and
most
important
honor
it's
legend
of
live
award.He
is
not
only
the
only
country
artists
ever
to
win
this
award
he
is
the
only
country
artists
ever
to
be
nominated,
other
artists
who
have
won
include(
Paul
McCartney,Stevie
Wonder,
The
Rolling
Stones,
Micheal
Jackson,
etc.).</p>








<p>On
June
1,
2013,
Strait
appeared
in
<a
href="/wiki/The_Alamodome?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Alamodome"
class="mw-redirect">The
Alamodome</a>
before
seventy
thousand
fans
in
the
last
concert
of
the
first
half
of
his
two-year
farewell
tour.
<a
href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Governor
of
Texas">Governor</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Rick_Perry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rick
Perry">Rick
Perry</a>,
who
was
in
attendance
with
First
Lady
<a
href="/wiki/Anita_Thigpen_Perry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anita
Thigpen
Perry">Anita
Thigpen
Perry</a>,
announced
that
henceforth
May
18,
Strait's
birthday,
would
be
&quot;George
Strait
Day&quot;
in
Texas.<sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>




</div>
